<div id="review_289518301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289518301" />
    <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington"><img alt="Jonathan Terrington" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478230200p2/6313408.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289518301?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Terrington" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Terrington" href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan-terrington">Jonathan Terrington</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141181479" href="/book/show/304266.The_Chrysalids">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">classic readers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=classic-literature">classic-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=classic-challenge">classic-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi-challenge">fantasy-sci-fi-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan-terrington?shelf=personal-favourites">personal-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289518301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15555331209689753135"><br/>Having recently read John Wyndham's famous novel <i>The Day of the Triffids</i>, which is known more for the film adaptations, I decided to read another of Wyndham's books. The result left me very satisfied and I must conclude that Wyndham now holds a place on my (imaginary) bookshelf of favourite classic sci-fi authors alongside Wells, Asimov and Verne to name a few.<br/><br/>The idea of <i>The Chrysalids</i> is simple but executed extremely well. As a result <i>The Chrysalids</i> is a complement to the aesthetic as well as </span>
  <span id="freeText15555331209689753135" style="display:none"><br />Having recently read John Wyndham's famous novel <i>The Day of the Triffids</i>, which is known more for the film adaptations, I decided to read another of Wyndham's books. The result left me very satisfied and I must conclude that Wyndham now holds a place on my (imaginary) bookshelf of favourite classic sci-fi authors alongside Wells, Asimov and Verne to name a few.<br /><br />The idea of <i>The Chrysalids</i> is simple but executed extremely well. As a result <i>The Chrysalids</i> is a complement to the aesthetic as well as to the mental senses of the reader. This is what I believe Wyndham excels at doing like Wells, creating compulsive and entertaining science fiction which is as readable as it is intelligent and questioning. Like all great novels this book ties to both the past, the present and the future of its readership and humanity.<br /><br />The plot follows one adolescent boy, David, growing up in a kind of post-apocalyptic world where an event named 'the Tribulation' has occurred. It becomes clear that this 'Tribulation' has affected the genetic make up of the population of the world. The very name of this event reveals another side to the story, a strict legalistic form of Christian religion has formed a new kind of community. In this community mutation is intolerable, a 'deviation' from man as the 'true image' of God. Of course the protagonist David recognises the fallacy of viewing mutants as inhuman:<br /><br />"Well, every part of a definition is as important as any other; and if a child doesn't come within it, then it isn't human, and that means it doesn't have a soul. It is not the image of God, it is an imitation, and in the imitations there is always some mistake. Only God produces perfection, so although deviations may look like us in many ways, they cannot be really human. They are something quite different."<br />I thought that over.<br />"But Sophie <i>isn't</i> really different - not in any other way," I told him. <br /><br />As it turns out David is himself a 'deviation', one of those 'sent by the devil' to test the true images. He, and a small group of his friends in the community, can communicate via telepathy. Of course no one can tell visibly that they are 'non-human' and so they remain hidden. That is until one of their number decides to marry a deviation-hating 'norm'.<br /><br />The issues this novel tackles are broad and far reaching. It is both a challenge to strict Pharisaic religion, which does not heed the true message of its source, and a tale about humanity. It questions what it is to be human: whether it is about appearance or about deeper, underlying issues. And as part of challenging what it is to be human it challenges how we alienate and accept others as alien and non-human: whether that be on race, gender, sexuality, religion, age or so on. The voice of the narrator, the protagonist is perfect for allowing the writer to speak on these issues. Take the following quote for example: <br />"'Oh,' I said, vaguely but safely. It was odd, I felt, how many people seemed to have positive, if conflicting, information upon God's views."<br /><br />Ultimately though this book was written years ago I believe it applies to today as an excellent novel we can learn from. I would encourage anyone to make sure that they read this book at least once. It may not necessarily be the best written of John Wyndham's books but it is one that challenges issues still relevant to our present and future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15555331209689753135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1083545228" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083545228" />
    <a title="El" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83144-el"><img alt="El" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479156984p2/83144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083545228?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="El" class="user" itemprop="url" name="El" href="/user/show/83144-el">El</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781590172926" href="/book/show/2460478.The_Chrysalids">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=biddles">biddles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=20th-centurylit-late">20th-centurylit-late</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=nyrb-editions">nyrb-editions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=science-fictiony">science-fictiony</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83144-el?shelf=society-went-boom">society-went-boom</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083545228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8363367652506021046">I nominated this book for my real-life book club because I was trying to think of something that would fit a Halloween-sort-of theme, and some description I saw of this book mentioned the Devil, so why not?<br/><br/>Sorry, book club. Not very Halloween-y, eh? And, apparently (at least in Pittsburgh), really difficult to find. I failed you all this month.<br/><br/>It is a post-apocalyptic novel, though, and I'm usually down for that. This particular post-ap novel is also a coming-of-age story, which I have to admit </span>
  <span id="freeText8363367652506021046" style="display:none">I nominated this book for my real-life book club because I was trying to think of something that would fit a Halloween-sort-of theme, and some description I saw of this book mentioned the Devil, so why not?<br /><br />Sorry, book club. Not very Halloween-y, eh? And, apparently (at least in Pittsburgh), really difficult to find. I failed you all this month.<br /><br />It is a post-apocalyptic novel, though, and I'm usually down for that. This particular post-ap novel is also a coming-of-age story, which I have to admit surprised me. That's (again) what I get for going into reading something without knowing a dang thing about it. The coming-of-age-r is David Strorm, the eldest son of a religious nut in Waknuk, more commonly known to us as Labrador. (It's in Canadia.) It's a few thousand years in the future after things went boom, and this whole community is just as zealous and fanatical as David's father. They believe (as many do) that humans are made in God's image, blah blah blah, and this community holds that to the very letter. "Normality" is very important to these folks, and since there was a global nuclear war and there's been a lot of crazy shit floating around, it's not uncommon for someone to be born... <i>not</i> normal. And this community is not going to go for that.<br /><br />There's a lot of discussion here about what makes one "normal" or "not normal". A few times felt a bit tedious, but I understand the point Wyndham was trying to make. It's an important issue for the community and one they do not take lightly. And, again, they're fanatical and if there's one thing fanatical people do it's be fanatical and not shut up about things.<br /><br />Everything else is pretty much a spoiler, so you'll just have to read it yourself if you're remotely interested.<br /><br />It's not my favorite post-ap novel but I feel it's a sci-fi classic and a great contribution to post-apocalyptic writing. It's a quick read (ringing in at just 200 pages) which is good because like a jackass I had to order a copy online because my beloved library system failed me on this one, and then the Internet failed me and I thought I wasn't going to get the book until November 4th. But the Internet also surprised me by arriving this past weekend, and I was able to get through most of it in just a couple of days (and then couldn't finish the last 10 pages until tonight because Life). Way to toy with my emotions, Internet.<br /><br />The ending does leave a bit to be desired. It was a little... weak? Disappointing? I cannot quite put my finger on it, but I feel slightly dissatisfied in the end which is a shame. I have seen a few reviews where this was make-or-break sort of ending, but I wouldn't be so extreme as to say it ruined the entire experience for me. I was fascinated and interested throughout the story, and that's really what's important to me.<br /><br />I would also take a moment to reflect on the author's name which, originally, is <i>not</i> just John Wyndham like a regular schmoe. His real name was... (wait for it...) John Wyndham Parkes Lucas Beynon Harris. Guy had more names than Dumbledore.<br /><br />Someone have a baby and name him Beynon, please and thanks.<br /><br /><br />Also: The NYRB cover is fucking amazing. LOOK AT THOSE COLORS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8363367652506021046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2065479845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2065479845" />
    <a title="Hákon Gunnarsson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson"><img alt="Hákon Gunnarsson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474574814p2/20498454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065479845?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hákon Gunnarsson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hákon Gunnarsson" href="/user/show/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson">Hákon Gunnarsson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12585859-the-chrysalids">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=british-literature">british-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20498454-h-kon-gunnarsson?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065479845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7825727520960641879">This was a bit different from The Day of the Triffids, (the only other John Wyndham novel I have read) and a bit similar as well. The Triffids is set during an present day (at the time of publication that is) apocalypse, while The Chrysalids is a post apocalyptic novel set in the future. The plot of both center around characters that are in the run, thought I think it takes longer until that part begins in The Chrysalids. Most importantly for me, I liked both of them.<br/><br/>It's an interesting read at </span>
  <span id="freeText7825727520960641879" style="display:none">This was a bit different from The Day of the Triffids, (the only other John Wyndham novel I have read) and a bit similar as well. The Triffids is set during an present day (at the time of publication that is) apocalypse, while The Chrysalids is a post apocalyptic novel set in the future. The plot of both center around characters that are in the run, thought I think it takes longer until that part begins in The Chrysalids. Most importantly for me, I liked both of them.<br /><br />It's an interesting read at this point in time when distrust for science seems to be increasing, and religious fanaticism Seems to be on the rise. Most of the action takes place in a society built up on a relegious fundamentalism. Wyndham paints a rather believable picture of that society. The science fiction elements of the story are not very visible, and I was even starting to think they would be comepletely absent, but then it take a turn into more science fiction like territory.<br /><br />What this book seems to be about is tolerance towards difference, because the way the society is set up in this novel, but the ending makes that reading a little more ambiguous. I'm still not sure what Wyndham meaning with it was exactly. Still, I think it is a very interesting science fiction novel with a good dose of suspence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7825727520960641879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2477542849" />
    <a title="Ilana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59371159-ilana"><img alt="Ilana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563253235p2/59371159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2477542849?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilana" href="/user/show/59371159-ilana">Ilana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/10295023-the-chrysalids">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=great-britain">great-britain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59371159-ilana?shelf=folio-society">folio-society</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2477542849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18294504992506449305">I lost a lot of sleep because of this book. Simply couldn’t put it down. A puritanical society where any deviation from strict codes of what constitutes normality and thus “godliness” and which destroys everything deemed “deviant” in which a boy born with all the right numbers of fingers and toes and all outward appearances perfectly acceptable, but with a terrible secret to hide: the gift and curse of telepathy which he shares with a small group of other children, which they must hide at all co</span>
  <span id="freeText18294504992506449305" style="display:none">I lost a lot of sleep because of this book. Simply couldn’t put it down. A puritanical society where any deviation from strict codes of what constitutes normality and thus “godliness” and which destroys everything deemed “deviant” in which a boy born with all the right numbers of fingers and toes and all outward appearances perfectly acceptable, but with a terrible secret to hide: the gift and curse of telepathy which he shares with a small group of other children, which they must hide at all cost.<br /><br />Written in the 1950s, we are given to understand they are living like early colonizers in a post-nuclear world where nature continually offers strange mutations, and nightmarish, unnameable things lurk in the Fringes. Somehow still terribly relevant, and more so than ever in this Trumpian dystopic reality show we are all presently living, because isn’t MAGA all about returning to the values of the postwar era? Which makes me think the return of some form of McCarthyism can’t be too far away... 😰<br /><br />Whatever your political or philosophical leanings, it’s a great yarn with an ending that can be read in many ways and leaves you thinking long after you’ve turned the last page.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52892004?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon" href="/user/show/1071724-simon">Simon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141181479" href="/book/show/304266.The_Chrysalids">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1071724-simon?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52892004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13052010944908733221">A post apocalyptic world in which society puritanically tries to resist the <i>deviations</i> that beset their crops, livestock and people through genetic mutations. <br/><br/>David Strorm, never quite understanding his father's fervour for normality soon discovers that he (and certain others) deviate from the norm in a new and undetectable way. As they try to keep their difference hidden and try to be normal, they eventually discover that they won't ever fit in and with the arrival of David's sister Petra, it b</span>
  <span id="freeText13052010944908733221" style="display:none">A post apocalyptic world in which society puritanically tries to resist the <i>deviations</i> that beset their crops, livestock and people through genetic mutations. <br /><br />David Strorm, never quite understanding his father's fervour for normality soon discovers that he (and certain others) deviate from the norm in a new and undetectable way. As they try to keep their difference hidden and try to be normal, they eventually discover that they won't ever fit in and with the arrival of David's sister Petra, it becomes impossible to maintain that illusion.<br /><br />This story is an allegory for social change in Britian in the 1950's. It explores the tension between the social forces for change and conservatism. It also incorporates the fear of nuclear attack and genetic mutation as well as the science of genetic manipulation.<br /><br />I found this to be an engaging and enjoyable read marred only slightly by a couple of plot niggles and an inevitably (unfavourable) comparison to the way Theodore Sturgeon handled a similar theme.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer660492048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8845184163481369940">I usually have a three book rule which states that I only read three consecutive books by <i>any</i> author. It's mostly to stop me from getting bored. Not so with Wyndham. I'm four in and still wanting more. I haven't read the Chrysalids since I was a youth, and, understandably, a lot of the evolutionary/religious themes were lost on me back then. It's a much richer reading experience now. As usual with Wyndham, this is a story which raises all manner of questions regarding what constitutes perfection</span>
  <span id="freeText8845184163481369940" style="display:none">I usually have a three book rule which states that I only read three consecutive books by <i>any</i> author. It's mostly to stop me from getting bored. Not so with Wyndham. I'm four in and still wanting more. I haven't read the Chrysalids since I was a youth, and, understandably, a lot of the evolutionary/religious themes were lost on me back then. It's a much richer reading experience now. As usual with Wyndham, this is a story which raises all manner of questions regarding what constitutes perfection, whether God concerns himself with definitions imposed by society, and the small minded approach of religious zealots. A book which only improves with age.</span>

And the best thing about this book is that it features my favourite kind of fictional characters: wise children with telepathic power!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2396516624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396516624" />
    <a title="Ana-Maria Petre" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36340154-ana-maria-petre"><img alt="Ana-Maria Petre" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573299057p2/36340154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396516624?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana-Maria Petre" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana-Maria Petre" href="/user/show/36340154-ana-maria-petre">Ana-Maria Petre</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396516624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9200791361316805626">I love clever science fiction because it is far more close to being philosophical than scientific or even fictional. A few more examples from this category are Ray Bradbury's" Fahrenheit 451" , R. A. Heinlein's" Stranger in a Strange Land" and Isaac Asimov's "I, Robot". As in the case of Wyndham's book, they all pose very interesting ontological questions and do not limit themselves to being novel or shocking. <br/><br/>Now, I know there was a golden age when science fiction had only been invented and fly</span>
  <span id="freeText9200791361316805626" style="display:none">I love clever science fiction because it is far more close to being philosophical than scientific or even fictional. A few more examples from this category are Ray Bradbury's" Fahrenheit 451" , R. A. Heinlein's" Stranger in a Strange Land" and Isaac Asimov's "I, Robot". As in the case of Wyndham's book, they all pose very interesting ontological questions and do not limit themselves to being novel or shocking. <br /><br />Now, I know there was a golden age when science fiction had only been invented and flying spaceships and alien invasions were all the domain of the new, so that this type of writing prospered. But today it's really hard to invent anything new "out there", so the only thing perpetually perplexing and new that we can always return to is ourselves. Scientific fiction without the philosophical (human?) element is bland and outdated. But this book is not one of those. <br /><br />Pleasantly readable and refreshing throughout, it is definitely a first read that has encouraged me to seek out more by this author. (I actually recently got another novel of Wyndham's, "The Midwich Cuckoos", which promises to be at least as interesting.) Genetic mutation is not a new subject, but the weaving of biblical themes, ethics and metaphysics into the tapestry of the novel resulted in quite an interesting mix. The main question of the book is what makes a man, man. Is it the likeness of God? <br /><br />"And God created man in His own image."<br /><br />But no one has actually seen God. One can only come up with their own projected image of God, and inevitably, this projection will be closest to themselves:<br /><br />"And God decreed that man should have one body, one head, two arms and two legs: that each arm should be joined in two places and end in one hand: that each hand should have four fingers and one thumb: that each finger should bear a flat finger-nail...Then God created woman, also, in the same image, but with these differences, according to her nature: her voice would be of higher pitch than man's: she should grow no beard: she should have two breasts..."<br /><br />The only problem? People are different. So each race and culture is bound to see a different God, according to their own image. We can only infer what follows from centuries and centuries of history that have all shown the same outcome: persecution. <br /><br />"And any creature that shall seem to be human, but is not formed thus is not human. It is neither man, nor woman. It is a blasphemy against the true image of God, and hateful in the sight of God."<br /><br />Another interesting theme is evolution and refusal of change. The species bound to disappear are those refusing to evolve, because the world is constantly changing and not adapting to it can bring only destruction. Man's arrogance makes him a master of refusal:<br /><br />"They stamp on any change: they close the way and keep the type fixed because they've got the arrogance to think themselves perfect. As they reckon it, they, and only they, are the true image; very well, then it follows that if the image is true, they themselves must be God: and, being God, they reckon themselves entitled to decree, 'thus far, and no farther.' That is their great sin: they try to strangle the life out of Life. "<br /><br />But anyone with a minimum knowledge of religion must know that God retaliates...<br /><br />"They weren't God's last word like they thought: God doesn't have any last word. If he did, He'd be dead. But He isn't dead, and He changes and grows, like everything else that's alive. So when they were doing their best to get everything fixed and tidy on some kind of eternal lines they'd thought up for themselves, He sent along Tribulation to bust it up and remind 'em that life is change."<br /><br />Replace God with Nature if you wish. That is not relevant. But this book it is nonetheless a powerful case against race pride, intolerance and any kind of groupism based on on thinking ourselves better than the rest. In the face of tornadoes, or God, if you will, we are all the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9200791361316805626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_134531292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Petra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1733683-petra"><img alt="Petra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314283484p2/1733683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra" href="/user/show/1733683-petra">Petra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134531292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6127888204124481124">I've read this book many times over the years and always enjoy it.<br/>The post-apocolyptic life where people are afraid to repeat the past and keep themselves in a simpler, more natural world, where perfection is all. One can banish those with deformities that can be seen but what can one do to protect oneself (and society) from deformities that one cannot see? <br/>The suspense and intrigue carries through to the end. </span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134804162" />
    <a title="Marianna Neal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13007653-marianna-neal"><img alt="Marianna Neal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572593566p2/13007653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134804162?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marianna Neal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marianna Neal" href="/user/show/13007653-marianna-neal">Marianna Neal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141181479" href="/book/show/304266.The_Chrysalids">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13007653-marianna-neal?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13007653-marianna-neal?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13007653-marianna-neal?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134804162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13253129036080027600"><b>3.5 out of 5 stars</b><br/><br/>This was my first John Wyndham book, and though I can't say I loved it, I am definitely interested in reading more of his work. This particular post-apocalyptic setting is very interesting, but the characters took a while for me to get into, and the second half of the book was more engaging than the first. Overall, I enjoyed it and would recommend it to fans of post-apocalyptic fiction.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WLcKHMre9T59k1VEAuSBTCOm/IFz7ZTnOrua0f62iMRikWPOcYA8Vtq44SX1EYuT9fkbSb1gGoBhxdxgM/V6Xg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GipPXSXPsBukoYH3Jb5aGvE61TYPbN/WtZsjPwRCevcgDCaPnpF5cwOKNZbSS1DFJ2Uy/sHhUbHu5WWOyQGIbQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36332.John_Wyndham">About John Wyndham</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3346276857498918184">John Wyndham Parkes Lucas Beynon Harris was the son of a barrister. After trying a number of careers, including farming, law, commercial art and advertising, he started writing short stories in 1925. After serving in the civil Service and the Army during the war, he went back to writing. Adopting the name John Wyndham, he started writing a form of science fiction that he called 'logical fantasy'. </span>
  <span id="freeText3346276857498918184" style="display:none">John Wyndham Parkes Lucas Beynon Harris was the son of a barrister. After trying a number of careers, including farming, law, commercial art and advertising, he started writing short stories in 1925. After serving in the civil Service and the Army during the war, he went back to writing. Adopting the name John Wyndham, he started writing a form of science fiction that he called 'logical fantasy'. As well as <i>The Day of the Triffids</i>, he wrote <i>The Kraken Wakes</i>, <i>The Chrysalids</i>, <i>The Midwich Cuckoos</i> (filmed as <i>Village of the Damned</i>) and <i>The Seeds of Time</i>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3346276857498918184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
